## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size. This is the core problem of population dynamics, where various ecological mechanisms (resource limitation, cooperation, predation, seasonal effects) shape the functional form of the growth rate.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Time-dependent Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-varying rate)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth kinetics)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth with linear death)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Time-decaying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (logistic with time-varying carrying capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- dP/dt proportional to P indicates per-capita growth rate is the key quantity; factor out P and model the per-capita rate separately
- Negative quadratic term in P (i.e., -P²) signals intraspecific competition and carrying capacity limitation
- Positive quadratic term at low P combined with negative cubic term suggests Allee effect with eventual saturation
- Logarithmic dependence on P (e.g., log(K/P)) indicates Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically
- Rational forms like P/(1+cP) arise from Holling Type II functional responses or contest competition
- Periodic functions of time (sin, cos) multiplying growth terms indicate seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where c≠1) suggest allometric scaling of metabolic or reproductive rates with body/population size
- If dP/dt = 0 at multiple nonzero P values, the model has multiple equilibria suggesting bistability (Allee effect or regime shifts)
- Exponential functions of time modulating growth parameters suggest environmental degradation or improvement trends
- Product form P*(K-P) naturally enforces two equilibria (P=0 and P=K) and is the hallmark of logistic-family models

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
$$0.8678(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185)P + 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) = -1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P^2/(6.058 \times 14.185)$$

Multiply by P:
$$= -P + P^2/14.185 + P^2/6.058 - P^3/(6.058 \times 14.185)$$

So the full GT becomes:
$$0.8678\left(-P + P^2/14.185 + P^2/6.058 - P^3/85.91\right) + 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P$$

The $-0.8678P$ and $+0.8678P$ cancel! So:

$$GT = 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P^2(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - 0.8678 P^3/(85.91)$$

This simplifies to:
$$GT = a \cdot P^{1/3} + b \cdot P^2 + c \cdot P^3$$

where $a, b, c$ are specific constants. The GT is a function of **P only** (no dependence on t).

So the GT has the form: **P^(1/3) + P² + P³** (with specific coefficients).

Now let me check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** $c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P^3 + c_2 P^2 + c_3 \exp(c_4 t)$ — Has $t$ dependence via $\exp(c_4 t)$. Setting $c_4=0$ gives constant $c_3$, but GT has no constant term. Setting $c_3=0$ eliminates it. Then we get $P^{1/3} + P^3 + P^2$. ✓
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Same as 1 but with extra $c_5$. Setting $c_3=0$, we get $P^{1/3}+P^3+P^2+c_5$. Extra constant — must be 0. Can set $c_5=0$. ✓
